B003ZSJ212|4.0|Alright, we need to simplify what people's problems with this set are. It apparently isn't the quality of the video (for the most part) or audio, which is what blu-ray enthusiasts care about and is what I ultimately bought a high-def tv and surround sound system for. It's basically the fact that George Lucas did not restore the theatrical versions of the original trilogy for blu-ray and only gave us slightly modified special edition versions with this set.     By now you already know what was changed, and there are some things which probably shouldn't have been touched, but they were and there's nothing we can do about it at this time. Now the question we have to ask ourselves is do we care more about the Star Wars experience on blu-ray, the medium that gives us the ultimate home theater experience, or are we so determined to stand by our convictions that the theatrical cuts should be included that we will shun this set and wait until it's released with the original theatrical cuts?    The answer to this question is actually simple, and it took me having to watch the original theatrical cuts on dvd to realize how ridiculous my original reaction was. As I watched these great movies on my 50\\" Pioneer Elite in Dolby 2-channel stereo, I couldn't help but feel underwhelmed in some way. I have this amazing home theater system, and these original theatrical cuts, with their grainy picture, black outlines around the special effects, and 2-channel stereo, which still sounded great for only 2 channels, simply don't give us the home theater experience we hoped for when we purchased all these expensive components. I began to realize that even if these versions were restored for blu-ray, it would look horrible because the level of detail on blu-ray would expose all the limitations in the special effects of that day. These cuts were meant for a lesser medium, like dvd or laser disc, where they could still showcase detail, but not enough where the limitations would be obvious anddistracting. And what is the point of Dolby Stereo, which was the original theatrical audio source, on blu-ray? Sure the special editions were widely criticized for the many changes that were made, but one thing is for sure, even though the special effects of 1997 seem dated compared to today's special effects, they are leaps and bounds ahead of the special effects from 1977, 1980, and 1983, and undoubtedly showcase on blu-ray better than the theatrical cuts ever would.    What seems to be apparent when you read all the negative reviews is that people are just angry at George Lucas for the changes he's made to his works over the years. I agree it seems annoying for him to make so many changes, but this is his story, Luke Skywalker is his version of himself in his sci-fi fantasy, and he went through a lot to simply get the original movie made. Star Wars doesn't just belong to him, and it doesn't just belong to the fans who made it popular, it belongs to everyone, and it is available in so many different formats to please all these different people. This blu-ray set was made for the people who want the ultimate Star Wars experience, and this is the ultimate experience that George Lucas envisioned himself. He made some changes to try to make it perfect for blu-ray, and sometimes we try a little too hard to make things perfect when they already are, but he's not doing it to make the fans angry, he's doing it FOR the fans, because he wants them to see the vision that he saw in his mind over 35 years ago. I don't know why people get so angry at him for that, without George Lucas we would not have this legendary work of art. It's still available in it's original form on dvd, but George Lucas is providing us with something he believes is better, something he believes is the pinnacle of the Star Wars experience, and I think that's awesome. I haven't even bought the set yet because I simply don't have the money, but as soon as I do, I will add this blu-ray set to my collection.    So if you want the ultimate Star Wars experience, this is it, and if you want to see the original theatrical cuts, you still can on dvd, and they're just as, if not more, entertaining as the special editions. You have to come to accept that if you want the original Star Wars theatrical experience, it's simply not blu-ray caliber, and if you want the ultimate Star Wars experience, it's going to be different than what you remember, but it's still Star Wars, and it's still as amazing as ever. People have this expectation that somehow we can create this perfect version of Star Wars that pleases George Lucas and the fans, but that will never happen, and that is why they've given us so many different versions. So decide for yourself whether you want the blu-ray experience with what many reviewers say is the greatest home audio experience and the best picture you've ever seen from Star Wars, or whether you want to stick to your guns and your laser disc and dvd versions just because they are the original theatrical cuts. When you think about it, this argument is trivial, if you love blu-ray and Star Wars, just buy it, and most likely you won't regret it.

However, being a big fan of all the previous Opeth material, I can't help feeling at least a little hesitant about fully embracing Heritage not knowing if this is a permanent change.  If they released, say, a companion \\"heavy\\" album, as with Deliverance and Damnation, maybe more of the older fans would be heaping as much praise on this as they did Damnation, knowing they still have the heavier side of the band to enjoy. 1594481717|5.0|I went to college wanting to become a doctor.  But though biology and medicine fascinated me, I couldn't find the passion for it that I wanted to have. That passion was waiting for me in my English classes, which annoyed me. I didn't want an English degree because I didn't want to write or teach professionally. I spent several semesters trying to avoid it, the study of English and literature eventually drew me in. I ended up with a Bachelor of Arts degree in English.    The four years since graduation have been a slow reconciliation between me and the degree I earned. I recently came across Daniel Pink's book A Whole New Mind and it inspired in me new optimism and pride for my English degree.    A Whole New Mind argues that with the developed world's new widespread abundance and automation, along with the rise of Asian world powers, we're entering a new post-Information Age. The book refers to this new era as The Conceptual Age. This new age will place (or is already placing) new emphasis on six human attributes in the workplace that can't be readily emulated by a computer or outsourced to cheaper labor on the other side of the world.    These attributes are design, story, symphony, empathy, play, and meaning.  All six are associated with the right hemisphere of the human brain, the region associated with creativity and feeling--as opposed to the left hemisphere's tendency towards logic and linear structure.    Pink gives each of the six traits its own section in the book.  As an English major, I was most excited by the story section. Pink points out that throughout human civilization, facts and information have been valuable commodities, but in the Information Age, facts and information were digitized and are therefore cheap and readily accessible.  As a result, our minds now require context to understand and utilize these data.  This context can also be called story.    As in the other five sections, Pink has a few anecdotes that support his insistence on story'snew importance in the professional world.  My favorite bit of evidence is 3M executives taking story-telling classes to become better leaders and more efficient communicators.  Pink also points out a new movement in medicine that encourages doctors to get to know their patients' individual stories as a means of strengthening communication and making treatment more effective.    I enjoyed the entire book, but I was especially interested in the story section because I believe I have a propensity and talent for story that I could only wish to have with science and medicine.    The six traits highlighted by Pink are not entirely separate--they form a creative and non-linear whole that is markedly different from the left-brain thinking that was of primary importance for our society up to and through the Information Age.  But as Daniel Pink demonstrates, we're advancing in a new direction that requires new ways of thinking.  I'm not yet sure how I'll be able to participate in this new age, but after reading A Whole New Mind, I'm thrilled to find out.

B005COO1X6|4.0|I read King's Mile 81 last night and thoroughly enjoyed it. Readers are split on this one, I don't ever think I've seen reviews more evenly divided between the stars than this short story. Leave it to King to even know how to manipulate what should be a bell curve!    Mile 81 leads us into familiar King territory, the secret world of kids. One reviewer went on and on about how kids would do this and wouldn't do that. Well, that reviewer is clueless. He or she may know how kids act when adults are around, but none of us knows what happens when they are with each other. It's true . . . And, frankly, I don't care because King creates a child's world that I believe. My ex used to play a variant on Paratroopers from Hell as a boy and has the scars to prove it. And listen to boys when they don't know they are being overheard, it is eff-this and eff-that as they flex their fledgling man-muscles. And as the proud possessor of my very first hangover at age 12, the thought that a boy would say, \\"yuk\\" at the bottle of vodka is wishful thinking at best.    And that is the crux of this tale. The monster was defeated because three children saw it for what it was and believed it to be what it was. Adults just kept lining up, as symbolized by the traffic jam on the off-ramp (one Expedition, pick-up with a trailer, abandoned gre-en Prius and a man-eating Ford or Chevy . . . sung to the tune of 12 Days of Christmas). And because adults had to believe there was a rational explanation (after all, they are adults) they kept being eaten. It didn't have to be a car. It could have been a thinny, a Venus Fly-Trap or a portable black hole. The car was a prop. Nothing more. Adults were eaten because they had lost their belief in monsters.    Enter the two young children who watch their parents disappear into the maw of the car. They knew the truth and the truth was monstrous. Five dead adults later, a 10-year old listens to the story told by the youngsters and sees the logic. Only a monster could do such a thing. Ergo, the car is a monster. However, in true \\"boy\\" fashion, he couldn't leave it alone. Calling back to The Body and IT, the boy just has to see the dead kid, just has to play in the Barrens, and just has to run up and touch the door of the haunted house. The magnifying glass is a trope. Nothing more. He wanted to have a story to tell the Raiders. He had wanted to show off his prowess with a magnifying glass and been dismissed. What better story than to focus it on a monster? And it worked. My only complaint was that it worked a little too well. I would have rather had a puddle of stinky goo for the adults to muse over while the kids knew the truth.    I never understand the constant rage in reviews about character development in plot-driven stories like this. What did you need to know about Bible guy or horse lady other than they were really tasty. It was their cars in the conga line on the off-ramp that moved the story along, not their personalities. The theme of this story (and oh how I loathe themes) was the fundamental difference between adults and children and how sometimes that difference is deadly. Well done to my fav writer and I loved the sneak peek at the JFK thriller.  PS: Why comment about a Stephen King comment about Sarah Palin that is irrelevant to this story. Other than, there is a monster not even King could dream up.

B0054PET3K|4.0|Kasabian return with album number 4 the weirdly titled \\"Velociraptor\\", so it should come as no surprise that this is one of Kasabian's most ambitious albums to date, not bad for a band that has seen lazy journalism call Kasabian, Oasis clones and labelled them lad rock. While Kasabian might share some of Oasis confidence and swagger their music has always been more closely linked to Primal Scream, Happy Mondays, The Stone Roses and even 70's glam rock. A quick look back at their 3 previous albums would show a band not scared to experiment with different styles and sounds.   The album opens with \\"Let's Roll Like We Used To\\" which sees songwriter Serge Pizzorno looking back at the early days before they made it big. It's a good start to the album. On \\"Days Are Forgotten\\" the track starts off with some big beats and a funky groove and features some lyrics that have a nice dig at their critics. There's the brilliance of the Beatles-esque sounding \\"La Fe Verte\\" which is sung by Pizzorno. Add that to Kraftwerk sounding \\"I Hear Voices\\" and it shows that Kasabian are willing to experiment in as many styles of music as possible.   The title track \\"Velociraptor!\\" is a big sounding stomp that has Tom spitting out his lyric's, not to many bands could pull off a song about a dinosaur with out sounding stupid. There's the epic \\"Acid Turkish Bath (Shelter from the Storm)\\" which at over 6 minutes long sounds like Kashmir era Led Zeppelin. The album features two big tracks that are made for playing live the brilliant \\"Re-Wired\\" with its big chorus and the beat driven \\"Switchblade Smiles\\" a song that won't full be appreciated until it's played live.   With the deluxe edition you get the full near 2 hour show from the O2 in Dublin, Ireland from November 2009, it's mixed in full surround as well. The Deluxe Edition comes in a white box set and contains the lyrics of all the tracks as well as poster of the black artwork of the album. One drawback of the white is that it marks really easy so it's best to handle with care!  With every album kasabian seem to make another stride musically, and \\"Velociraptor!\\" is no exception. Moreover, even Atkins now talks about the important difference of good fat and protein, from say fish, versus fat and protein from beacon.  I felt that the jab at the other diets was much more ideological than that of the \\"objective scientist\\" we are told in the book.<br /><br />From a clinical perspective, I have seen almost all of the diets work! However, it is a book I would place right alongside all the other diet books on my shelf.<br /><br />For the record, my favorite and the one that has possibly had the greatest impact on my own personal health is:  Power Up Your Brain, by Perlmutter and Villoldo. 0307277887|3.0|There is a lot of hype surrounding Darkly Dreaming Dexter. It has some very high praise by a lot of critics out there. There is an ongoing award-winning TV series based off it, which I have not seen. So, when I delved into Dexter's smooth narration, I didn't know what to expect. As we all know, most books with this amount of hype around them don't turn out to be as good.<br /><br />Darkly Dreaming Dexter is about a serial killer and a blood spatter analyst who works for the Miami Metro Police. Problem is, they are one and the same. By day Dexter is a charming nerd, and by night his Dark Passenger leads him as he hunts for his prey. But he doesn't kill just anyone. He only kills people who are guilty of murder. He never kills the innocent.<br /><br />Emotionless, Dexter walks the earth fully aware of his own inhumanity. He doesn't have a conscience, but he does have a code, created for him by his father.<br /><br />It's safe to day that Darkly Dreaming Dexter has a clever premise, to say the least. At first I didn't know how comfortable I'd feel rooting for a serial killer, no matter how his actions were justified. But Lindsay doesn't take the route of trying to explain away Dexter evil deeds. He embraces them. Dexter (who narrates the story) is fully aware of what he is doing. It's the fact that he has no emotions that keeps him from caring. He does it only to fulfill his need to kill.<br /><br />At the same time, he's a very likable character. It might be that we, as the readers, see glimpses of humanity flicker across his eyes every so often, but he's just plain likeable. He likes kids, and he does hold a place in his heart for his stepsister Deborah Morgan (he was adopted) who also works for Miami Metro. It's little things like that that allows us to care for this quirky and horrifying character that is Dexter. The fact that he narrates the story as well I think adds to it as well.<br /><br />But I think the aspect that solidifies us caring about him, is the factthat he struggles. It's not his fault he's like this, after all. Something happened in his past, but he (and we) doesn't know what it is. He can't help it. The need to kill (what he calls the dark passenger) is always lurking in the back of his brain, and he must kill to satisfy it.<br /><br />Now that I've gone over Dexter's character in depth, and we now that he is a very interesting and compelling one, I'd like to go over how he is developed, and how the story he is in works.<br /><br />Firstly, I'd like to give Jeff Lindsay due credit for creating this fascinating character that defies the clichd run-of-the-mill cardboard cutouts we have all too often today. Plus he does a great job of setting of the premise of the story in which Dexter is placed. He sets up a quirky bunch of side characters, and a gritty location. The atmosphere is ripe, and the tension is high as Dexter tries to juggle the various aspects of his life (did I tell you he has a girlfriend so that he can fit in?).<br /><br />But as the story progresses... that's just it. The story progresses. Nothing more. Dexter continues to be a contemplative emotionless self, the side characters bumble around, and the only real interaction is between Dexter, Deborah, and Detective LaGuerta, who works with Miami Metro. Yes, there certainly is a complex touchy relationship between the three of them, but it never really goes anywhere.<br /><br />In a book like this where the central idea is the main character, not the plot, you have to develop your characters and have your characters' relationships develop as well.<br /><br />On the flip side, it seems Lindsay, at the same time, moves Dexter along too quickly. He is described as cold and logical. Never subject to stupidity and anxiety of the human race. So we're told. But that's all. Jeff Lindsay doesn't show us this. We're shown, later on Dexter changing from his normal routine. But we haven't even seen him in his routine yet, so why should we be surprised when he breaks the routine? In the specific instance I'm referring to, Dexter does something very horrifying and quite disgusting. It does nothing to make him a more likable person.<br /><br />Over the course of the book I found myself caring less for Dexter, and getting rather annoyed with him. Toward the end there is a conflict where he is about to let down his sister, something that would result in a very bad thing (I don't want to spoil anything). I found this completely unbelievable. Over the course of the book Dexter constantly says that while he doesn't love, per se, he would never let his sister down. And this, for once, is shown, not only told. Lindsay puts the only relationship we care about at risk, and not by outside forces.<br /><br />Lindsay really rushed the climax of the book. This is the result of undeveloped characters and plot. The book should have been a hundred pages longer. That way, Lindsay could have kept a good pace, taken his time to develop solid characters, and made the ending not only believable, but also satisfying.<br /><br />In the end, all we get is a really great set up of both characters and plot, and loads of potential along the way with possible a redeeming aspect to it, but all of this is wasted. Before I go, I would like to say that I did like the writing style. I thought it worked very well for the book, and was highly entertaining. It makes me even more sad to give Darkly Dreaming Dexter a poor review.

B005ER6SNM|5.0|Where do you even start with a review for this movie? This might not even qualify as a \\"review\\" in the typical sense. Well to explain my \\"paradigm\\" from which I'm coming from, let me say i've always had a fascination with violence and \\"disturbing content\\" on film and in the media. So I've seen a lot of \\"horror movies\\" but also a lot of other weird things. I've explored the worst of the worst but virtually never is there a film where violence is used to inflict really, really soul-scarring damage. That is because, you see, most \\"extreme\\" violence films are what I would call \\"Trashy\\". This can refer to the poor quality of their presentation, but more often it refers to an attitude about violence. Violence used for entertainment, I think, is perfectly okay and sometimes very awesome. On the other hand, violence as a tool to evoke a different emotional effect has an entirely different effect on us as a viewer. And I have always been interested in those latter kinds of things. I don't know why. Humans have always had that curiosity, they just externalize it differently.<br /><br />Most of the \\"most disgusting/violent/disturbing movies\\", according to the internet, are actually in this \\"trashy\\" category, so they aren't _really_ all that disgusting or violent or disturbing. They are just dumb and do not create an emotional effect beyond something superficial and shallow. Often they are just bad movies so they generate contempt for wasting anyone's time. They certainly do not create a real sense of HORROR or TERROR. And you know, I have always wanted to find the pinnacle of _really_ disturbing/violent films for years now.<br /><br />That movie is definitely _A Serbian Film_, without any doubt. I will not discuss the story at all or refer in detail to any specific scenes. I don't even really think anyone should watch this movie, and you can go read more about it elsewhere. I'm not really here to make this movie sounds interesing so that you go watch it, and honestly the basic premise is pretty clever so if I avoid that issue it's probably for the best.<br /><br />But I will say -- without hesitation but still feeling a bit weird about it -- _Serbian Film_ is a MASTERPIECE. It is the scariest film of all time, easily. The way it creates an emotional attachment, establishes an atmosphere of utter, paralyzing dread, and its escalation from one unbelievably devastating, brutal, and shocking scene to another, is really, really effective. This movie really really, really terrifying. In terms of craftsmanship, the filmmakers really deserve credit. They know what makes a good horror film, and then they just raised the intensity and brutality to infinity and beyond. The level of depravity and cruelty inflicted upon people in this movie is really unimaginable to the average person. Your heart will feel like it's going to explode about halfway into the film... and then it gets way worse. I almost couldn't bear to see what was going to happen in the end (although it's somewhat predictable, which actually makes it WORSE as the end approaches), but I did and it sucked. No, the ending did not suck in the sense that it was \\"bad\\", because it was a good ending in terms of climactic narrative, but in the sense that it BAD -- like \\"that's the worst thing I can ever imagine happening\\" kind of BAD.<br /><br />Some people will jump in at this point and say, \\"Oh well it can't be as bad as X\\". No, shut up. You don't know what you're talking about. It's way, way worse than X. I promise you, I have seen all those obscure movies you scour google for days and weeks to find. \\"Oh but have you seen--?\\" Yes, I've seen it. \\"But i bet you haven't seen--\\". No, _i've seen that too_. And it's mostly trash.<br /><br />But here is why this movie is not \\"trash\\". First of all, it is extremely well made. The acting is very effective, the writing is sharp (even with some nice moments of tenderness and humor early on). But most importantly the story, which is probably not very realistic or anything, is completely absorbing and it makes the viewer care. We can appreciate the main character's situation. He seems to be a likable dude. We want good things to happen to him and his family. But, then he is lured in by what seems to be a good opportunity and becomes quite literally enslaved to evil. Our empathy becomes horror magnified a thousandfold by the fact that we give a damn, and by the unbelievable intensity of evil perpetrated -- manipulating someone into doing something they would never do, something that is so vile that even talking about it will make you puke.<br /><br />It almost makes you forget that you are watching this movie because it's supposedly the \\"nastiest ever\\" and not because it's just a good movie. Almost. But then it beats you like a sledgehammer as a good movie AND the nastiest.<br /><br />And yet here is the paradox. This is not really a good movie, like \\"I recommend this\\" or \\"I would watch this again.\\" In that sense, it is the worst movie. But because it is the best worst movie, it is actually amazing. But your soul will be shattered when you watch it. The ending is literally the most horrible thing ever on film. I will certainly never, EVER watch it again. Just thinking about it makes me feel bad. But I cannot deny that it is incredibly powerful on its own terms, and it has to be taken seriously. This is not like our normal horror movies where violence is really part of the fun. But here with _Serbian Film_, you dread violence like you do in real life. That is a powerful effect and I can count the number of movies like that on one hand. All possible goodness in this movie is utterly broken, corrupted, and destroyed by the end, through abject violence. Your soul bleeds into the ether as the credits roll.<br /><br />Is this movie \\"deep\\" or interpretative on some level? I don't know. Maybe it doesn't matter. \\"This is a diary of our own molestation by the Serbian government... It's about the monolithic power of leaders who hypnotize you to do things you don't want to do. You have to feel the violence to know what it's about.\\" Those are the words of the director. Take them for whatever they're worth. Indeed, truly horrible things happen to people in real life. Real horror is real people dying and suffering and being forced to do awful things with real consequences. In that sense, this movie is not that bad. No one died. No one got hurt. No actual children were exposed to anything inappropriate. But by drawing on some a real sense of loss and tragedy and horror they grew up with, the filmmakers create a really powerful horror film. I find that interesting.<br /><br />My heart is racing just thinking about this movie. I feel like i could faint. Why did I even write this review? It makes no sense, i gave it 5-stars saying no one should see it and you will be scarred by it and probably react negatively _even if you normally dig this stuff_. Seriously. I could give it one-star and have the same content for this review. Another reviewer somewhere said it best, \\"You don't want to see this movie. You only think you do.\\" Be careful. You can't go back in time and un-watch this movie after you watch it.  And so in seeing _A Serbian Film_, my quest for the most violent and disturbing film of all time is over. After seeing this movie, I am reduced to spending the rest of my days watching nice happy things like episodes of \\"Sailor Moon\\".rbing and it makes the viewer care. I'll address the strengths and weaknesses of Miss Morgenstern's freshmen debut and leave the judgement up to you.    Strengths:  Concept: The world of the Night Circus takes place during the late 19th century and early 20th century. When a mysterious circus enters the town without warning, all flock to it and gaze upon the illusions and black and white decor. A spellbinding world where magic appears to be one thing when it's something else entirely.    Description: I'm divided on the description Morgenstern employs throughout the book. It's beautifully worded and filled with enchanting similes, but sometimes those similes border on pompous and confusing. More down to earth phrasing or comparisons could have helped but I'll grant her the concession it would break the novel's illusionary theme and imagery if she didn't employ it.    The Circus: The upside to the Night Circus is the circus itself. In some stories the city or setting acts as a main character. With magic abound in every corner, dark and melancholy secrets swirling behind the scenes, Morgenstern masters atomsphere and a place you want to come back too.    Weaknesses:    Plot: Unforunately, The Night Circus's primary plot fizzles due to the focus on the Circus through it's fluff descriptions. The main characters, the two dueling magicians, don't have much in term of development or depth. The romance is stiff. There's subtleness to it with their apprecation of each others's magic gifts consisting of their \\"courtship\\" in the first half. Marco throughout the story employs what one reviewer mentioned as fireworks. There's little sense of suspense and the ending leaves me dissastified overall.     Prose: Part of the problem is the present tense 3rd person and the choose your own adventure 2nd person for the parts Morgenstern describes to you. In a sense, you are a background patron to the Circus throughout these descriptions. It breaks the immersion of the novel, for me at least. And the present tense lacks the power of the past tense. The long descriptions don't reach purple prose but the novel could have been cut by 50-100 pages of what some writers call fluff. Self-indulgent description about every little detail that's superflous to the plot and characters hurts the novel.    note: This is my own bias showing through. I prefer the iceberg principle employed by Hemmingway. Not the short choppy sentences but rather letting the reader fill in the blanks on certain secondary elements to create a sense of mystery and wonder about the Circus.     Characters: There are too many to count. Characters fade in and out of the background and share the cryptic and mysterious archetype too often. The protagonists show potential but with their fates tied to the competition, it doesn't allow for many \\"quiet moments\\". The kind of character building conversations and scenes where the action moves at a methodical pace and still keeps the plot moving. There are certain gem characters that stand out but they're underutilized.    Morgenstern deserves accolodes for her concept and setting. She still has a long way to go in terms of characterization and plot but that's the point of sophmore novel. Writing a smash hit freshman novel is rare; and the Night Circus casts an enchanting illusion that  doesn't last long enough for the reader to give their time to it. I give it a 3/5.

B0055S348W|5.0|PrintShare is worth having if you want to print directly from your phone or tablet. You have a lot more control over output if you email or transfer your documents to a PC but PrintShare shines when you need to print certain content (call logs, messages, calendar entries, contacts) for which transfer may be difficult and output quality is not an issue.<br /><br />A few brief additional remarks:<br /><br />- PrinterShare adds a sometimes needed capability because, unlike more mature and much larger operating systems, Android does not support printing natively - after all, who would have thought 2 years ago that people may want to print 'stuff' off their phones or tablets?<br />- Not being integrated into the operating system explains PrinterShare's peculiar behavior. Instead of printing from within an app or by selecting 'print' from an object's list of available properties and actions, PrinterShare runs as a separate app that provides print support for a defined set of apps/objects: pictures, web pages, calendar, contacts, messages, call log, Gmail, Google docs and documents. In other words, you must run PrintShare every time you want to print something.<br />- The app supports Wi-Fi, Bluetooth, remote printers and cloud printers. Of these I tested the first 2 without problems. My printers were located and identified quickly, drivers were loaded and the output quality (printer's default) was good. However, the drivers ability to control a printer did not go much beyond sending the doc to the printer. Cloud and remote printing may provide additional flexibility but I haven't tested them.<br />- I had no problem printing images, PDF, Word and text files on an Epson Artisan and an HP OfficeJet Pro printer but I don't know how many or which specific printers are supported or which printers are not supported.<br /><br />Given that the app adds a needed capability to the operating system I can't hold the its developers responsible for lack of deep integration with the OS. This would not be needed if Android provided print support itself. The app's inability to fully control printers is also no surprising given that PrintShare's publisher has limited resources. Its limitations noted, this should be a 5-star for anyone who must be able to print off an Android device.<br /><br />--<br />>> Brush your teeth, it's the law! &lt;&lt;provided print support itself. B004GCKRWY|4.0|Movie hunk Ryan Reynolds stars in this film as Paul Conroy, an outside contractor operating a truck in Iraq. After an attack which leaves his friends dead, he awakens in a crude coffin with a butane lighter and a cell phone which is not fully charged. So begins this movie that is essentially telling the story of Conroy being held hostage for a hefty ransom while waging a battle against time to be rescued and dealing with increasingly irrational captors.<br />Given that Reynolds is the only actor that the audience sees during the film and that his stage is his cramped coffin/wood box, he manages to do a great job as the anxiety filled captive struggling to be rescued. And herein lies my problem. This movie is a nightmare for anyone who is claustrophobic. Reynolds did such a great job adapting to his film environment that I had a problem not feeling confined.<br />The script was clever and not completely predictable. At one point while Reynolds is in a frenzy to be located (remember he has no idea of exactly where he is because he didn't come to until he was already buried) the company he contracted with goes through a protracted process of firing him over his ebbing phone signal so they won't bear any responsibility regarding his kidnapping. While I had a problem with a couple aspects imbedded in the script, this was a taut thriller that managed to be suspenseful and terrifying.
B005E7AOHI|3.0|I've been a fan of Primus since seeing the video for John the Fisherman and saying to myself \\"What the hell is that guy doing to that bass!\\" I won't say I'm a die hard, but I appreciate this bands quirks and musical chops. That being said, Green Naugahyde just isn't what I wanted to hear after Primus being away for so long.  Despite my awe at Claypool's playing, I don't really care for his other work; I find them wanky and self indulgent. Primus is usually a good compromise between experimentation and listenability.  My biggest problem with this CD is that there isn't a good standout track that really grabs your attention. There isn't a John the Fisherman, or Tommy the Cat, or My name is Mud, or Anti-Pop here; it all moves along at the same pace. Some bands don't set out with the intent of writing singles, but if you listen to Sailing the Seas of Cheese or Anti-Pop, there are a lot of good memorable songs without them necessarily being written as just singles. This album reminds me more of a Tales From the Punchbowl or Brown Album, which from both albums I can only name one song of note.  My second problem is the production. Primus has been into producing their own stuff for a while, probably to maintain creative control. While the recording doesn't sound cheap like the Brown Album, it just isn't mixed very well. The bass is clunky, the vocals are too quiet, and Jay Lanes excellent drum work doesn't have any pop. Of course Larry's guitar is lost somewhere in the background, but that's usually the case. I personally think his best performance was on Anti-Pop. Les has apparently fallen in love with combining overdrive, bass synth and auto-wah, but it muddies his playing and gets old fast.   The highlights of Green Naugahyde are Jay Lanes drum work and the lyrics. Primus isn't known for direct social commentary, their lyrics are usually more whimsical, but this CD has some pretty harsh words for modern pop culture. I like it!    The bottom line is that hardcore Primusfans or Les Claypool worshipers will love this album. It's definitely Primus, which is still better than 70% of what's going on in the musical world today. I would have personally liked to see them do something what was more inline with Anti-Pop.
